# INST — Index Rerum Faciendarum

**Status:** ACTIVE
**Created:** 2026-03-20
**Authority:** META — System-wide governance instrument
Purpose: Universal hanging index of things to be done — the canonical gap between what the system IS and what it NEEDS TO BE. (961 items, 21 domains)

> *Index Rerum Faciendarum* — after the classical scholarly apparatus: *Index Locorum* (places), *Index Nominum* (names), *Index Rerum* (things). The gerundive *faciendarum* transforms reference into obligation: not things that exist, but things that must be made to exist.

### The Four Indices

This document is the first of a four-part classical index apparatus for ORGANVM:

| Index | Latin | Purpose | Status |
|-------|-------|---------|--------|
| **Index Rerum Faciendarum** | *Things to be done* | Universal work registry — the gap between IS and NEEDS TO BE | **THIS DOCUMENT** |
| **Index Locorum** | *Index of places* | Canonical map of where everything lives — repos, directories, files, URLs, infrastructure endpoints, deployment targets | IRF-IDX-001 |
| **Index Nominum** | *Index of names* | Registry of all named entities — organs, repos, tools, agents, personas, regimes, orders, specifications, dissertations, people | IRF-IDX-002 |
| **Index Rerum** | *Index of things* | Ontological inventory of what exists — every artifact, its type, its state, its relationships, its provenance | IRF-IDX-003 |

Together, the four indices constitute a complete scholarly apparatus for the system: where things are (Locorum), what they're called (Nominum), what they are (Rerum), and what remains to be done (Rerum Faciendarum). The first three are reference instruments; this one is a governance instrument.

---

## How to Use This Document

This is a **living governance instrument**, not a snapshot. Every session that produces or discovers work items should update this index. The auditor (`vigiles_engine/auditor.py`) and the omega scorecard (`organvm omega status`) are the primary automated consumers.

**Update protocol:**
1. When a session closes, add completed items to `## Completed` with session ID and date.
2. When new work is discovered, add to the appropriate organ section with priority and source.
3. When work is blocked, move to `## Blocked` with blocking reason.
4. When work becomes irrelevant, move to `## Archived` with reason.

### Completion Logging — External Index Propagation

**REQUIRED:** When work is completed, it MUST be logged not only here but across ALL external indices with an interest. Every completion triggers this checklist:

| # | External Index | When to update | How |
|---|---------------|----------------|-----|
| 1 | **This document** (IRF) | Always | Move item to `## Completed` with session + date |
| 2 | **GitHub Issues** | If a GitHub issue exists for this work | Close the issue with comment referencing commit SHA + IRF ID |
| 3 | **Omega Scorecard** | If the work advances an omega criterion (#1-#19) | Run `organvm omega status` to verify; note criterion state change |
| 4 | **Inquiry Log** | If the work completes/advances an SGO research commission | Update `praxis-perpetua/commissions/inquiry-log.yaml` |
| 5 | **Testament Chain** | If the work is a significant system event (new module, repo, governance change, deployment) | Verify with `organvm testament status` |
| 6 | **Concordance** | If the work introduces or retires governance IDs | Update `docs/operations/concordance.md` |
| 7 | **Registry** | If the work changes repo state (new repo, status/tier change, new edges) | `organvm registry update` |
| 8 | **Seed contracts** | If the work changes repo capabilities, dependencies, or event subscriptions | Update the repo's `seed.yaml` |
| 9 | **CLAUDE.md** | If the work adds/changes modules, routes, tools, commands, or architecture | Update the repo's CLAUDE.md hand-written sections |
| 10 | **Companion indices** | If the work creates new locations (Locorum), names (Nominum), or artifacts (Rerum) | Update the relevant companion index when built |

Not every completion triggers every index. A P2 doc fix may only need #1 and #9. A new engine module needs #1, #2, #5, #7, #8, #9. Use judgment — but the DEFAULT is to check all 10 and consciously skip inapplicable ones, rather than unconsciously miss applicable ones.

**Priority tiers:**
- **P0 — NOW**: Human-gated or zero-cost unblocking actions. Do today.
- **P1 — SOON**: Next-session work. Clear path, no blockers.
- **P2 — GROWTH**: Extends existing capability. No deadline pressure.
- **P3 — HORIZON**: Future work. Requires design or prerequisites.

### DONE-ID Allocation Protocol

**DONE-NNN IDs are globally unique.** Concurrent sessions have caused 3 collision incidents (DONE-298, DONE-302, DONE-372/373). To prevent future collisions:

1. **Before assigning any DONE-NNN**, read `data/done-id-counter.json` to get `next_id`.
2. **Claim your range**: increment `next_id` by the number of completions you need.
3. **Commit and push the counter file FIRST**, before using the IDs anywhere in the IRF.
4. **If the push fails** (non-fast-forward), `git pull --rebase`, re-read the counter, reclaim from the new ceiling, try again.
5. **Then** use your claimed range in the IRF statistics and item rows.

The counter file is the single source of truth for the DONE-ID ceiling. The statistics section is a human-readable summary — it is NOT the authority for the next available ID.

| IRF-SYS-217 | **P2** | **Agent config files unsourced behind XDG-redirect symlinks — Universal Rule #2 inversion (config-class, not artifact-class).** Sibling to SYS-216 (axis question) and SYS-215 (Codex work-artifact stores), but the failure-class is distinct: this concerns *runtime config files* (`~/.codex/config.toml`, `~/.gemini/settings.json`, `~/.gemini/policies/housekeeping.json`), not *historical work artifacts*. Losing a config = silent agent-behavior change in production; losing a work artifact = lost history. **Empirical surface (this session 2026-05-27, daily-hook-drift v2 generalization):** chezmoi maintains `~/.codex` and `~/.gemini` as **symlink-spec** entries (`symlink_dot_codex` → `~/.local/share/codex`, `symlink_dot_gemini` → `~/.local/share/gemini`) — the symlink itself is sourced but everything *under it* escapes chezmoi tracking by design (XDG_DATA_HOME convention treats it as runtime data, not source config). `chezmoi add ~/.codex/config.toml` fails with `not a directory` because chezmoi looks for `symlink_dot_codex/private_config.toml` and finds a 30-byte symlink-spec file. Three configs in this topology: Codex `config.toml` (15K), Gemini `settings.json` (2.5K, MCP server registry), Gemini `policies/housekeeping.json` (1.4K). All present on disk, none in chezmoi-source — Universal Rule #2 inversion. **daily-hook-drift v2 routine (shipped this session in domus `1d85832`) correctly reports these as dormant** ("3 unmanaged" in stderr), so the matrix auto-activates when remediation lands. **Closure options:** (a) move configs to XDG_CONFIG_HOME (`~/.config/codex/`, `~/.config/gemini/`) and have agents read from there — requires per-agent reconfiguration; (b) carve specific files out of the symlink escape — chezmoi `include` directive or per-file symlink_ prefix; (c) accept dormancy and add to the "documented Universal Rule #2 inversions" list (similar to `/Users/4jp/CLAUDE.md` local-only carve-out per IRF-CRP-011/DONE-532); (d) per-config inline-render via `.tmpl` files that the agents source at runtime. **Related:** SYS-210 (parent IRF, this v2 routine is mitigation expansion), SYS-215 (work-artifact sibling), SYS-216 (axis question — applies to this class too). ### Cross-Cutting Concerns (from SGO research programme)

These are not discrete tasks but organizing principles that cross-cut the entire programme:

| ID | Concern | Description | Scope |
|----|---------|-------------|-------|
| IRF-RES-CC1 | Syntactic/semantic boundary | All governance automation must respect the Rice boundary — every check is either syntactic (decidable) or semantic (undecidable, requiring human judgment) | All organs, CI, governance |
| IRF-RES-CC2 | Governance Trilemma universality | The trilemma applies at every level: system, organ, repo, and governance tool; each level makes its own choice; choices must be coordinated | META, ORGAN-IV, all organs |
| IRF-RES-CC3 | Naming as infrastructure | Every naming decision is an ontological commitment that shapes organizational topology; naming debt compounds; naming governance = API design rigor | All repos, conventions, docs |
| IRF-RES-CC4 | Measurement constitutes its object | CI checks, governance scores, and quality metrics constitute quality, not merely detect it; assessment design must optimize constitutive alongside diagnostic value | All CI, scoring, governance |
| IRF-RES-CC5 | Human-in-the-loop is structurally necessary | Human judgment at the semantic boundary responds to impossibility results (Godel, Tarski, Rice, Goodhart), not a stopgap; the human is the incompleteness response | IRA panel, promotion, AI design |

| IRF-OPS-051 | **P2** | **`organvm context sync --dry-run` writes to disk while printing `[DRY RUN] No files were modified.`** Empirical 2026-05-17 during post-`/compact` Phase 4 close-out cascade. Reproduction: from `/tmp` with target repo's working tree clean, `ORGANVM_ADDITIONAL_WORKSPACE_ROOTS=~/Code/organvm:~/Code organvm context sync --dry-run` printed `Updated: 246, Created: 3, [DRY RUN] No files were modified.` Verification: post-run `git diff` in `~/Code/organvm/sovereign-systems--elevate-align` showed `CLAUDE.md`/`AGENTS.md`/`GEMINI.md` all mutated with mtime in the run window, reverting the deliberate IRF-CRP-014 trim (commit `7714b0f`). Restored via `git -C <dir> restore CLAUDE.md AGENTS.md GEMINI.md` loop across 75 git-tracked dirs (2 special cases handled: corpvs Code-clone newly-created untracked AGENTS+GEMINI deleted; domus chezmoi-source CLAUDE.md restored; 5 NOT-GIT dirs left intact with their auto-block markers refreshed). Likely root cause: `organvm_engine.contextmd.sync.sync_all()` passes `dry_run` to `_inject_section(...)` but the section-injection path does not gate the actual write call on the flag (or the gate is misplaced and only suppresses the post-write log line, not the write itself). The stdout `[DRY RUN] No files were modified.` is therefore a **false-success report** — same failure-mode family as IRF-OPS-050 (refresh silent-skip) and IRF-SYS-181 (chezmoi silent-enrollment-drift): the user-facing channel asserts a state that does not match disk. Damage potential is much higher than its siblings — `--dry-run` is the safety affordance users invoke specifically to AVOID writes when probing behavior; violating that contract turns the safest invocation into the most expensive. Operational impact this session: 240-file blast required ~5 min cleanup loop and 1 advisor call to confirm the cleanup pattern; had the user been less attentive, the trim of IRF-CRP-014 (CLAUDE.md bloat past 40K /doctor limit) would have been silently reversed across multiple repos. Closure options: (a) audit `organvm_engine/contextmd/sync.py` `_inject_section` and any nested write paths to confirm `dry_run` short-circuits BEFORE the file write, not after (estimated ~30 min including unit test that asserts no mtime change in a tmpdir under `--dry-run`); (b) add an integration test that runs `--dry-run` against a tmpdir fixture and asserts file SHA-256 unchanged pre/post (~20 min; defends against regression); (c) bundle with IRF-OPS-050 + IRF-SYS-181 closure under a single "loud-warn + correct-dry-run" PR since all three are user-facing-channel-lies in the same subsystem. Pairs with IRF-OPS-050 (sibling — silent-skip on path drift), IRF-SYS-181 (sibling — silent enrollment drift), IRF-CRP-014 (the trim this bug silently undoes), IRF-SYS-178 (system-wide autogen drift — this bug masks attempts to safely inspect what refresh would do). | IRF-SYS-186 | **P3** | **MEMORY.md and `reference_sibling_scopes.md` hardcode monotonically-growing counts that decay between updates — empirical drift of +349 plans, +10 scopes, +9 repos detected 2026-05-18.** Three hardcoded-count claims in the constitutional memory layer (plans count, sibling-scopes count, preservation-parity repo count) all monotonically grow; each was correct at write time and decayed to wrongness. | IRF-OPS-056 | **P2** | **Apple `/etc/zshrc:17` silently clobbers user HISTFILE/HISTSIZE/SAVEHIST in interactive shells; `SHELL_SESSIONS_DISABLE=1` does NOT protect against this assignment.** Empirical 2026-05-20: `~/.local/state/zsh/history` (declared XDG path in `~/.zshenv:38`) had 156 bytes untouched since 2026-03-03, while `~/.config/zsh/.zsh_history` ($ZDOTDIR/.zsh_history — Apple's clobber target) had 51 KB and active writes. Load order in zsh: `~/.zshenv` → `/etc/zshrc` → `$ZDOTDIR/.zshrc`. Apple's `/etc/zshrc:17` does a bare `HISTFILE=${ZDOTDIR:-$HOME}/.zsh_history` assignment (also drops HISTSIZE 50000→2000, SAVEHIST 50000→1000), which runs AFTER `~/.zshenv` and overwrites. Non-interactive shells skip `/etc/zshrc` and never trip this. `SHELL_SESSIONS_DISABLE=1` gates only the per-session block at `/etc/zshrc:99`, not the unconditional assignment at line 17. Fix shipped 2026-05-20 (chezmoi-source commit pending): added `dot_config/zsh/01-history.zsh` that re-asserts HISTFILE/HISTSIZE/SAVEHIST after `/etc/zshrc` runs (loaded via `for config_file in [0-9]*.zsh` in `$ZDOTDIR/.zshrc`). Verified: `zsh -i -c 'echo $HISTFILE'` now reports `/Users/4jp/.local/state/zsh/history`. Open follow-up: 51 KB stranded history at the wrong location is a frozen snapshot until user decides migrate/adopt/archive. Closure options: (a) implemented — `01-history.zsh` override; (b) migrate stranded history via `cat ~/.config/zsh/.zsh_history >> ~/.local/state/zsh/history` (~1 min, then null source); (c) leave as snapshot. | IRF-SYS-187 | **P2** | **`domus-memory-sync` lacks inter-session conflict resolution — concurrent Claude Code sessions can clobber MEMORY.md and plan files via last-writer-wins semantics; the structural gap is "no merge step before commit."** Empirical 2026-05-20: session 10300548 (fork-resume of 3a1287bc, PID 97820) held a stale in-memory copy of MEMORY.md while a separate active session (`9cb55c4d-3191-4b61-a8e8-192e4710affb`) wrote new entries. Each `domus-memory-sync` invocation from session 10300548 restored its stale state, clobbering the active session's updates. The race resolved itself when PID 97820 died during compaction (verified `ps -p 97820` empty post-compact). But the structural gap remains: any future concurrent-session pattern has the same race. The sync script does `git add <path> && git commit` with no merge or conflict-check step. Closure options: (a) sync script reads remote state first, fast-forwards local, then commits — adds ~200ms but resolves the race (~30 LOC); (b) per-session lock at `$XDG_STATE_HOME/domus/memory-sync.lock` with PID-aware staleness check — prevents simultaneous syncs but doesn't solve stale-state-in-memory (~50 LOC); (c) memory writes use append-only semantics so concurrent writes merge by Git rather than overwrite — semantic shift, requires reformatting MEMORY.md from single source of truth to log structure (high cost, durable); (d) accept the race and rely on user-side audit + Universal Rule #12 (memory = hypothesis, verify on read) — status quo. Closure (a) is the natural durable fix. Pairs with IRF-OPS-053 (sibling — `domus-memory-sync` silent-fails on bare invocation, same script different bug), IRF-SYS-181 (chezmoi enrollment-drift on directory moves — same script-blind-to-state-of-system pattern). | Agent | S-2026-05-20-terminal-shell-codex-hook-diagnostic, observed clobber pattern in cross-session MEMORY.md regression | None |

### S-2026-05-21-session-best-practices-audit Discovered Items (2026-05-21)

Session context: synthesis + plan + audit pass on session-content best practices across the five-agent fleet (Claude Code, Codex, Gemini, OpenCode, GitHub). The audit produced four findings whose remediation is non-trivial enough to warrant durable IRF rows. Two are structural gaps named at synthesis-time (G1, G2 below); two are operational deltas surfaced by the audit (B1, D1). Codified protocol lives at `~/_dot-config/health/session-best-practices.md`; audit at `~/_dot-config/health/session-best-practices-audit-2026-05-21.md`.

| ID | Priority | Action | Owner | Source | Blocker |
|----|----------|--------|-------|--------|---------|
| IRF-SYS-189 | **P2** | **No foreign-key cross-reference between four parallel work registries — atom registry (`prompt-atoms.json`, `ATM-XXXXXX`), plans (`~/.claude/plans/*.md` + per-repo `.claude/plans/`), IRF (this document, `IRF-XXX-NNN`), pipeline task queue (`organvm atoms pipeline --write && organvm atoms fanout --write`).** Each registry has its own identifier scheme; no join surface. Reconciliation is by inspection. `BACKLOG-AT-A-GLANCE-*.md` files at `data/prompt-registry/` are periodic snapshot attempts to compose a single graspable surface over all four — but they are snapshots, not joins. The "four parallel work registries" framing is distinct from the "four classical indices" framing in IRF-SYS-122 (Locorum / Nominum / Rerum / Rerum Faciendarum, where prompt-atoms is proto-Index Rerum). G1 names the WORK-registry FK gap; SYS-122 names the INDEX-architecture observation. | IRF-OPS-063 | **P3** | **`claude install <version>` does not prune prior versions — versioned binaries accumulate indefinitely at `~/.local/share/claude/versions/<v>` as ~200 MiB self-contained Mach-O arm64 executables, reachable only via the `~/.local/bin/claude` symlink. Multi-entry-point divergence is structural by design: Claude Desktop bundles its own copy at `~/Library/Application Support/Claude/claude-code/<v>/` (2.1.146 at audit, updated via Desktop releases); Antigravity IDE bundles its own at `~/.antigravity-ide/extensions/anthropic.claude-code-<v>-darwin-arm64/` (2.1.147 at audit, updated via IDE extension releases); the CLI is the only entry-point `claude install` manages. **Retention policy decision (this row's closure act):** keep N-1 as on-disk rollback target; prune N-2 and older on demand. 2.1.145 deleted this session (199 MiB reclaimed via `rm`); 2.1.146 retained as rollback if 2.1.147 regresses. Diagnostic shipped: `~/.local/bin/claude-health-check` reports CLI / Desktop / Antigravity versions, installed versions on disk, running claude PIDs by binary path, and divergence summary — read-only, on-demand, no daemon. Investigation chain at `~/Code/_agent/claude-local-application-support.md` (full report + truth-audit). Closure options: (a) one-shot prune of N-2 + `claude-health-check` diagnostic — shipped this session as the smallest-reversible-intervention BUILD step; (b) extend `claude-health-check` with a `--prune-n2` flag that auto-rm's the second-oldest version (opt-in destructive, one additional command) — deferred as YAGNI until cadence proves it; (c) wrap `claude install` in a `claude-safe-update` script that stops processes, installs, prunes, restarts — rejected as overengineered (restart-on-update promise unkeepable since restart ≠ session resume; Universal Rule #9 spirit); (d) periodic SessionEnd hook that prunes — rejected as on-demand-CLI-only principle (Universal Rule #9). (a) is shipped; (b) is a one-line addition if cadence justifies; (c)/(d) are rejected. **Lesson:** divergence across Desktop / Antigravity / CLI is structural-by-design, not a defect to monitor — each surface manages its own bundle on its own release cadence. The actionable scope is N-2 retention on the CLI surface alone; cross-surface divergence is a read-only observation. Pairs with `~/CLAUDE.md` "Never run `brew zap claude-code`" guard (same multi-entry-point fragility family, opposite failure mode — zap deletes the CLI rather than letting it accumulate). | User+Agent | S-2026-05-21-claude-version-sprawl-review, `~/Code/_agent/claude-local-application-support.md` (investigation + truth-audit), `~/.local/bin/claude-health-check` (diagnostic), `~/.local/share/claude/versions/` (verified state post-prune: 2.1.146 + 2.1.147 only, 403 MiB total) | None |

### S-2026-05-27-slash-command-namespace-convention — IRF-SYS-220 (2026-05-27)

| IRF-SYS-220 | **P2** | **Slash-command autocomplete is unwieldy — 165+ user skills + ~60 plugin commands flood `/`. Filename-prefix is the only sequencing lever.** Conductor observed: typing `/` queues a "massive unwieldy list." User-level commands at `~/.claude/commands/*.md` sort alphabetically by filename and live flat. Plugin commands use `namespace:command` syntax (e.g. `vercel:deploy`, `slack:standup`) — but that namespace is plugin-manifest-defined, not available to user commands. Subdirectory namespacing under `commands/` is undocumented; behavior unverifiable without risking live commands. **Closure approach shipped this session for the session-phase suite (commit `11973f7` on domus):** prefix-based grouping — 9 lifecycle commands renamed `/explore` → `/s-explore`, etc. Typing `/s-` filters to exactly the suite in autocomplete. Convention codified in `~/.config/ai-context/session-phases.yaml#agents.claude.namespace_convention`. **Broader closure options:** (a) audit + prefix-group the OTHER high-frequency user-skill suites (e.g., `/m-` for memory/maintenance, `/g-` for governance) — additive, low-risk; (b) prune rarely-used skills entirely from the user skill set (review usage logs; archive uncalled skills) — riskier but addresses root cause of "165 entries"; (c) propose to Anthropic: native command-categorization UI (favorites, pinning, fuzzy-match across description text) — feature request; (d) package the session-phase suite as a plugin to get proper `session:phase` namespace via plugin manifest — bigger refactor, but truest fit to the existing namespace pattern. (a)+(b) are conductor-actionable; (c) is upstream; (d) is medium-effort. Pairs with the chezmoi namespace-prefix convention established in `housekeeping-schema.yaml` and now `session-phases.yaml` — a per-agent declaration of how surfaces organize. | Agent | This session 2026-05-27 (`72318f10`) hall-monitor + rename pass; domus `11973f7` (the 9 s-prefix renames); `session-phases.yaml` `namespace_convention` field codifies the convention; conductor observation "/queue up a massive unwieldy list" | Conductor decision among (a)/(b)/(c)/(d). |

### S-2026-05-29-sync-false-green — DONE-562 (2026-05-29)

| **DONE-562** | SYS | **`sync-plans-to-session-meta` false-green telemetry fixed + plans-auto-sync subsystem put under version control.** The plans-mirror sync script (`~/.local/bin/sync-plans-to-session-meta`, the PostToolUse hook that mirrors agent `plans/` dirs into `~/Workspace/session-meta/`) wrapped every git call in `2>/dev/null \|\| true` and logged `COMMIT+PUSH: done` **unconditionally** — so `.sync-plans.log` asserted success while HEAD never moved. This masked TWO ~25-min mirror freezes in one session, caused by a 0-byte orphaned `.git/index.lock` (jetsam-killed git proc on the 16GB machine) that silently blocked every `git add`. **Fix (Rule #6, fix-the-base):** `commit_and_push()` rewritten to (1) self-heal an orphaned `index.lock` (age > 120s → remove; a real sync commits in < 2s, so older = unambiguously orphaned — auto-cleared instead of manual `rm`); (2) capture HEAD before/after and log the TRUE outcome (`COMMIT+PUSH: ok (<before> -> <after> pushed)` or a specific `ERROR:`/`WARN:`/`ABORT:` line, with real git stderr piped to the log). The whole plans-auto-sync subsystem is now durable + honest. | S-2026-05-29-sync-false-green |

### S-2026-05-29-post-commit-hook-finding-3 — DONE-563 + IRF-SYS-238 (2026-05-29)

| **DONE-563** | SYS | **DONE-561 post-commit hook: retry-on-empty-target (Finding 3 from /verify pass).** Post-/verify of DONE-561 found 1 of 60 hook dispatches recorded `SKIP-UNTRACKED` for `private_dot_claude/projects/-Users-4jp/memory/reference_jules_org_migration_2026_05_29.md` (commit `adfd478`, 15:55:22Z). At /verify time (~2h later) the same file IS chezmoi-managed and `chezmoi target-path` returns the correct runtime. **Diagnosis:** chezmoi's internal state index can lag the auto-commit cascade by milliseconds-to-seconds — `chezmoi add` → autoCommit fires → post-commit hook fires → `chezmoi target-path` queried — but chezmoi's state hasn't seen its own add yet. **Fix:** in `dot_config/ai-context/scripts/executable_chezmoi-source-post-commit-hook`, when `chezmoi target-path` returns empty, `sleep 1` and retry once before declaring `SKIP-UNTRACKED`. ### S-2026-05-29-cron-arm-exec-bit — DONE-564 (2026-05-29)

| **DONE-564** | SYS | **daily-operational-heartbeat cron armed + latent exec-bit/false-arm defect fixed (sibling to DONE-562; guardrail-gated work landed under explicit per-session authorization).** The prior session was structurally blocked (Rule #55 / public-ORGANVM push-auth) from arming the heartbeat and pushing corpvs/bound, and handed off a proposed one-liner. On explicit conductor authorization ("full permission; no destruction only evolution"), this session executed all three — but **verify-before-arm caught two latent defects the handed-off one-liner would have shipped:** (1) **`git add -A` would have conflated provenance** — corpvs's untracked set included prompt-registry archives keyed to *foreign* session UUIDs (`ba0dda23`, `e1f6bb64`) + a Gemini closeout; a blanket add+single-commit would have buried the DONE row among unrelated concerns. Split into 5 atomic corpvs commits (`e847fdc→f5ff372`): DONE-562 row alone, prompt-registry index+archives, Gemini closeout, layout-sweep plan resolution, residual auto-capture. (2) **`run.sh` was mode `-rw-r--r--` (non-executable)** — the proposed cron invoked it directly (`…/run.sh`), so it would have thrown `Permission denied` at 08:31 *daily*, and after 3 such fires the script's own kill-switch (`.failcount ≥ 3 → touch .disabled`) would have **silently and permanently disabled** the heartbeat. **Fix:** `chmod +x run.sh`; arm crontab idempotently (append-only guard, preserves existing entries) as `31 8 * * * …/run.sh >> …/cron.log 2>&1`; live smoke-test fired once → exit 0, ramp-safe dry-run confirmed (`.side-effects-enabled` absent ⇒ `--live` only, side-effects gated off), `.failcount` clean, not `.disabled`. **Ramp gate intact:** side-effecting routines stay dry-run until the conductor creates `~/.claude/scheduled-tasks/daily-operational-heartbeat/.side-effects-enabled`. Also landed the bound Claude→Codex handoff (`bcfef1e→8624d6d`). All 4 repos (domus/session-meta/corpvs/bound) verified 0/0 against remotes post-push. Architectural lesson: a handed-off shell one-liner is a *hypothesis* — exec-bit, file provenance, and target existence must be verified before arming an autonomous recurring process (Rule #8 validate-before-present + memory-is-hypothesis). | S-2026-05-29-cron-arm-exec-bit |

### S-2026-05-29-heartbeat-live-flip — DONE-566/567 + IRF-SYS-241/242 (2026-05-29)

| **DONE-566** | SYS | **`daily-operational-heartbeat` flipped to LIVE side-effects under explicit conductor authorization ("flip the heartbeat to live") — and the live-fire validation caught + fixed 3 latent defects the dry-run never could.** This is the second key of the ramp-safe two-key design: DONE-564 *armed* the cron (runs daily, dry-run); this creates `~/.claude/scheduled-tasks/daily-operational-heartbeat/.side-effects-enabled` so runs actually bite (`run.sh` line 25 flips `FLAGS` `--live` → `--live --allow-side-effects`, unlocking the 3 `side_effect:true` routines). **Live-fire validation surfaced 3 defects (all fixed, re-validated to rc=0 / 0 `[FAIL]`):** (1) **`memory-sync` registry command was a bare `domus-memory-sync`** — that script is hook/flag-mode only and *errors* on bare invocation ("bare invocation — use '--help'"). Fixed → `domus-memory-sync --all` (verified: syncs N files, rc=0). (2) **`prompts-distill` had a broken handoff** — registry ran bare `organvm prompts distill`, which reads `<atoms>/clipboard-prompts.json` that nothing generates → "Input file not found". Fixed by chaining its real precursor `organvm prompts clipboard` with **explicit aligned I/O paths** (the two commands' default filenames never matched — see IRF-SYS-241). (3) **leak-vector** — the clipboard export holds 1112 personal clipboard prompts (2.3MB); `clipboard`'s default `--output-dir` is CWD, so under cron (CWD=scheduler) or any tracked tree it would deposit personal data into a repo. **Rerouted** the handoff through a PRIVATE `~/.cache/organvm-heartbeat/` (neither git- nor chezmoi-tracked); added defense-in-depth `.gitignore` nets in BOTH `organvm-engine` (`ai-prompts-clipboard-export.*`) and public `corpvs` (`data/atoms/ai-prompts-clipboard-export.*`). Verified post-fix: export lands only in `~/.cache`, corpus + scheduler dirs clean (no leak). Final fire: `run.sh` rc=0, all 3 side-effecting routines pass (memory-sync ✓, atom-pipeline-refresh ✓ [7-step pipeline + 8-organ fanout], prompts-distill ✓ [clipboard 1112 prompts → coverage report]), `.failcount` clean, not `.disabled`. Registry fixes shipped at session-meta; gitignore nets at engine + corpus. Architectural lesson (extends DONE-564): a handed-off *registry of commands* is a bundle of hypotheses — each side-effecting routine must be live-fired before "armed" can be called "working." | S-2026-05-29-heartbeat-live-flip |
| **DONE-567** | SYS | **`organvm-engine` clipboard extractor crashed the entire extraction on a single NULL Paste.app timestamp.** Surfaced by DONE-566's prompts-distill fix: `organvm prompts clipboard` raised `TypeError: unsupported operand type(s) for +: 'NoneType' and 'int'` at `prompts/clipboard/extractor.py:71` (`datetime.fromtimestamp(ts + APPLE_EPOCH)` where `ts` is `None`). The SQL query filtered `WHERE d.ZRAWPASTEBOARDITEMS IS NOT NULL` but **not** on `i.ZTIMESTAMP`, so one Paste.app row with a null timestamp aborted ALL extraction → zero clipboard prompts. **Fix (root-cause, at the data-source boundary):** added `AND i.ZTIMESTAMP IS NOT NULL` to the WHERE clause, matching the adjacent null-filter idiom. Purely additive — those NULL-timestamp rows are unusable for the time-threaded narrative anyway, and previously produced *nothing* (crashed everything); now every valid row is recovered (1112 unique prompts extracted post-fix). Validated: 35 clipboard tests pass; `organvm prompts clipboard` rc=0. organvm-engine `src/organvm_engine/prompts/clipboard/extractor.py` + `.gitignore` (export-artifact net). | S-2026-05-29-heartbeat-live-flip |
| IRF-SYS-241 | **P2** | **`organvm prompts clipboard` and `organvm prompts distill` were designed to chain but their default I/O filenames never match — and clipboard's default `--output-dir` is an unsafe CWD-relative leak vector.** `clipboard` writes `ai-prompts-clipboard-export.json`; `distill` defaults to reading `<atoms-dir>/clipboard-prompts.json` — different name, different dir, so a bare `clipboard && distill` always fails on missing input. Worked around in the heartbeat registry (DONE-566) with explicit aligned `--output-dir`/`--input` paths through `~/.cache`, but that is a symptom-patch. Additionally, `clipboard`'s default `--output-dir` = current working directory means running it from any git repo deposits 1112 personal clipboard prompts into that tree — a standing leak vector for any caller, not just the heartbeat. **Fix base (Rule #6):** (a) align the engine defaults so `clipboard` writes exactly the filename `distill` reads (e.g. both default to `<atoms-dir>/clipboard-prompts.json`), letting them chain with no explicit flags; (b) change `clipboard`'s default output to a non-tracked cache/data dir (never CWD) so personal data can't land in a repo by default. | Agent | 2026-05-29 heartbeat live-flip: empirical path mismatch in run.log (`clipboard` → `…/ai-prompts-clipboard-export.json`, `distill` → `…/clipboard-prompts.json` not found); leak confirmed (export landed in corpus working tree from CWD-relative default before reroute). | Conductor: approve engine default-path alignment (a) + safe-default-output-dir (b); until then the heartbeat registry carries the explicit-path workaround + gitignore nets. |
| **DONE-568** | OPS | **`scripts/check-done-id.py` regex false-positive fixed — the DONE-ID validator was permanently red.** Closes the long-standing IRF candidate flagged in the prior closeout (and IRF-OPS-019 context): line-23 pattern `DONE-(\d+)` greedily captured `2026` from the date-form ID `DONE-2026-04-30`, yielding a spurious capture of `2026` that always tripped Check 1 (`2026 >= next_id`). The validator thus failed on EVERY run regardless of real ID hygiene — a permanently-red gate trains everyone to ignore it. **Fix:** `DONE-(\d{1,4})(?![\d-])` — the trailing negative lookahead rejects any DONE-number followed by a digit or hyphen, so date-form IDs (a separate, non-counter-sequenced scheme) produce no match while real numeric IDs (DONE-566/567) match cleanly. Verified: validator now passes (`781 IDs found, max=DONE-567, counter next_id=569`). Surfaced while validating this session's own DONE rows — a permanently-failing validator can't validate. organvm-corpvs-testamentvm `scripts/check-done-id.py`. | S-2026-05-29-heartbeat-live-flip |
| IRF-SYS-242 | **P2** | **`run-routines.sh` swallows per-routine failures — `run.sh` exits 0 and CLEARS `.failcount` even when side-effecting routines `[FAIL]`, so the `.failcount ≥ 3 → .disabled` kill-switch can never trip on them.** Empirical 2026-05-29: the first live fire had 2 routines `[FAIL]` (memory-sync, prompts-distill) yet `run.sh` returned 0 and cleared failcount. The kill-switch (run.sh:32-37) only fires on a non-zero exit from `run-routines.sh`, but the runner aggregates routine failures into log `[FAIL]` markers without propagating them to its exit code. **Consequence:** a routine that fails *every day* (as both did pre-fix) would fail silently forever — the heartbeat would look healthy (rc=0, never `.disabled`) while doing nothing. **Fix:** make `bin/run-routines.sh` exit non-zero if any `--allow-side-effects` routine fails (or expose a failure count the entrypoint checks), so persistent side-effecting failures escalate to the kill-switch. Must be done IN LOCKSTEP with IRF-SYS-241 / DONE-566 routine fixes (tightening the gate before the commands are correct would auto-disable the heartbeat after 3 days). | Agent | 2026-05-29 heartbeat live-flip: fire 1 had `[FAIL]`×2 but `run.sh rc=0` + `.failcount` absent (cleared); run.log boundary-marked fires confirm. | Conductor: approve failure-propagation in run-routines.sh; sequence AFTER the DONE-566 routine commands are confirmed reliably green in cron. |

### S-2026-05-29-substrate-decay-gaps — IRF-SYS-228/229/230/231/232 (2026-05-29)

| IRF-SYS-228 | **P1** | **No decay protocol declared per canonical surface.** Every substrate surface (skills, plugins, MCP servers, hooks, memory, plans, sessions, IRF rows, atoms, notifications, scheduled-task PRs) is born permanent with no expiration rule, no curator declaration, no archival cadence. Empirical evidence (2026-05-29 substrate audit): 935 IRF rows / 21 DONE (2.2% closure rate); 1,002 active plans in `~/.claude/plans/`; 14,898 open atoms; 3,597 agent session artifacts (573 Codex + 2,642 Gemini + 303 OpenCode + 79 Claude scopes). Closure rate ≪ creation rate at every surface = monotonic accumulation. **Fix:** extend Canonical Surfaces table in `~/.claude/CLAUDE.md` with two new columns: **Curator** (named owner with prune authority) and **Decay protocol** (explicit close/supersede/archive rule per surface). Pairs with IRF-SYS-224 (scheduled-task PR fold gap — first manifestation of this pattern). | Agent | 2026-05-29 substrate audit (session 38130932); cross-surface inventory at user direction "wholly and fully and from root to leaf"; 4-agent fleet substrate counts. | Conductor authorization on Canonical Surfaces table amendment + per-surface curator declaration. |

| IRF-SYS-235 | **P2** | **macOS `uchg` (user-immutable) flag silently blocks git operations across unknown number of repos.** Empirical 2026-05-29: `~/Code/organvm/a-i--skills/.git/` had recursive `uchg` flag applied to all `.git/*` entries (COMMIT_EDITMSG, config, description, FETCH_HEAD, gk, HEAD, hooks, index, info, lfs, etc.). ### S-2026-05-30-archive-idempotency-irf — IRF-SYS-243 (2026-05-30)

| IRF-SYS-243 | **P2 SHIPPED** | **`organvm session archive` CLI never surfaces the `force` flag the library already implements → a resumed-then-continued session's archived transcript freezes pre-merge with no supported refresh path.** Empirical 2026-05-29: session `c1ab249a` archived 18:13 as `cuddly-swinging-alpaca` (pre-merge snapshot); PR #91 (`fix(session): repair broken organvm session archive`) merged **18:55:37Z**, mergeCommit `4ef8b97` — 42 min *after* the archive froze. The archived transcript copy is therefore permanently pre-merge. **Verified root cause (engine source, HEAD `4ef8b97`):** `archive_session()` (`src/organvm_engine/session/archive.py:122-179`) *already* accepts `force: bool = False` and correctly bypasses the skip-guard (`if not force: if meta.session_id in state: … skip_reason="Already archived"`, lines 170-179) when `force=True` — the library capability **exists**. But the CLI handler `cmd_session_archive` (`src/organvm_engine/cli/session.py:586-604`) reads only `session_id/project/since/agent/dry_run/no_raw` and calls `archive_session(...)` **without `force=`**, and the subparser (`src/organvm_engine/cli/__init__.py:1334-1369`) declares no `--force`. So from the CLI — the only conductor-facing surface — re-archiving is impossible: `<id>` always hits skip-if-exists and returns `Skipped: Already archived`. **Fix base (Rule #6 — the library half is done, only the CLI wiring is missing, ~2 LOC):** (a) add `sess_archive.add_argument("--force", action="store_true", help="Re-archive even if already archived (refresh a stale snapshot)")` at `cli/__init__.py:~1369`; (b) thread `force=getattr(args, "force", False)` into the `archive_session(...)` call at `cli/session.py:600`. **Blast radius LOW (∴ P2 not P0):** the canonical durable records — git (`4ef8b97` merged) + memory (`domus 64d806f`) — already carry the full arc; the stale transcript is a convenience derivative, not data loss. **Distinct from IRF-SYS-240** (that row is the `session-auto-archive` *gate* coupling, G1/G3); this is the `organvm session archive` *command's* skip-if-exists with no CLI override — different code path, different defect. Pairs with IRF-SYS-240 (same `/s-09-archive` arc) and the Phase-2 SessionEnd-hook plan (archiving once at true session-end would make `--force` rarely needed but not redundant, since a session can still be resumed after its end-hook fires). | Agent | This session `a2033c40` (2026-05-30), picking up the held filing from prior session `fbd350ab` `/s-09-archive` close-out; verified against engine source at HEAD `4ef8b97` (read `archive.py:122-179` force param + skip-guard, `cli/session.py:586-604` no-pass-through, `cli/__init__.py:1334-1369` subparser lacks `--force`); PR #91 merge state confirmed via `gh pr view 91` (state=MERGED, mergedAt=2026-05-29T18:55:37Z, mergeCommit=`4ef8b978`). | Conductor: approve the ~2-line CLI thread-through (add `--force` arg + pass `force=` through). Optionally rule whether the SessionEnd-hook archive trigger (per IRF-SYS-240 "Also" note) is the durable answer that makes manual `--force` a rare-case affordance rather than the primary fix. **SHIPPED — closed by DONE-571 (engine PR #93 squash-merged `1d83404`).** |
| **DONE-571** | SYS | **IRF-SYS-243 SHIPPED: `--force` threaded through the `organvm session archive` CLI.** The library's `archive_session(force=False)` skip-bypass existed but was unreachable from the CLI; `--force` is now wired through BOTH paths so the flag is never a silent no-op: `cli/__init__.py` archive subparser gains `--force`; `cli/session.py` reads it and passes into `archive_session(...)` (single) + `archive_all(...)` (batch); `session/archive.py` `archive_all()` and `discover_unarchived_sessions()` gain `force`, with discovery dropping the already-archived filter (`if force or meta.session_id not in state`) when set. **Backward-compatible** — default (no `--force`) still returns `Skipped: Already archived`. **Verification:** 2 hermetic regression tests added (skip vs force-bypass) → 15/15 archive + 73/73 session suite pass; pyright 0 errors; `ruff` unrunnable locally (binary absent) → deferred to CI, which passed (test / test-matrix 3.11+3.12 / spec-compliance / secret-scan all green). **Behavioral proof via editable-install CLI:** `organvm session archive c1ab249a --force --dry-run` → `Would write: …/2026-05-29--cuddly-swinging-alpaca` (refreshes the exact snapshot that froze pre-merge in the original report), while the no-`--force` path still skips. ### S-2026-06-05-qa-audit-remediation — IRF-SYS-244 (2026-06-05)

| IRF-SYS-244 | **P2** | **`resolve_project_path` parent-fallback mis-roots session archives for removed-worktree sessions → archives + skip-guard state land in `<repo>/.claude/worktrees/.claude/sessions/`.** Empirical 2026-06-04 (session `613045ee`, heal-dehardcode lane, domus): the session ran in worktree `<repo>/.claude/worktrees/heal-dehardcode`, pruned its own worktree at closeout (correct hygiene), then archived — `meta.cwd` no longer existed, so `resolve_project_path()` (`src/organvm_engine/session/archive.py:60-77`) hit the "cwd might be a subdirectory that was removed — try parent" fallback (lines 73-75) and returned `<repo>/.claude/worktrees/` — a workspace-state container, not a project. Result: archive dirs (`2026-06-03--prompt-verified-the-worktree-already-exists/`, `2026-06-03--humble-giggling-narwhal/`) AND `.archive-state.json` written under `<repo>/.claude/worktrees/.claude/sessions/`; bit twice in one session; the misplaced `.archive-state.json` also splits the skip-guard state across locations (a later archive resolved from the correct root cannot see prior state). A naive parent-walk can never be right for worktree-homed sessions: the parent is by construction a state container, not a project. ### S-2026-06-05-g1-reconcile — IRF-SYS-245 (2026-06-05)

| IRF-SYS-245 | **P3** | **`session-auto-archive` G2 gate scans only `$HOME/.claude/plans` (maxdepth 1) → repo-scoped closeouts are structurally invisible, so a session that closed out correctly inside a repo still fails G2.** Empirical 2026-06-05 (G1-reconcile session in corpvs worktree `wip/g1-reconcile`): the bound `mcp-toggles` closeout that originated this reconciliation was repo-scoped, and `--check` failed `G2: no closeout-2026-06-05-*.md or 2026-06-05-closeout-*.md in /Users/4jp/.claude/plans` despite the closeout existing. **Verified root cause (script source, canonical home `~/.config/ai-context/scripts/session-auto-archive`):** the G2 block hardcodes `PLANS_DIR="$HOME/.claude/plans"` and `find … -maxdepth 1` over the two closeout filename grammars — no provision for per-repo `.claude/plans/`, per-project scope dirs (`~/.claude/projects/<scope>/`), or worktree-homed closeouts. The 2026-06-04 fix that taught G2 the second filename grammar did not widen the search roots. `emit_session_receipt` shares the same single-root assumption (same `PLANS_DIR` default), so DONE-gated receipts also miss repo-scoped closeouts. **Fix base (Rule #6):** widen G2's search roots — at minimum union `$HOME/.claude/plans` with the current repo's `.claude/plans/` (and plausibly the unified plan index from `build-unified-plan-index`, which already solves multi-root plan discovery) rather than patching per-path; apply the same roots to `emit_session_receipt`'s DONE-grep. Sibling of IRF-SYS-240 (G1/G3 coupling, SHIPPED via gate-independent `--on-session-end`) — G2 is the remaining batch-gate scoping defect; like 240's options (a)/(b), this only blocks the batch `--check`/`--archive` drift path, not the per-session SessionEnd hook. | Agent | This session (2026-06-05 G1-reconcile): `--check` output shows G1 ✓ / G2 ✗ with the quoted single-root message; script source read fresh at the G2 block (`PLANS_DIR="$HOME/.claude/plans"`, `find -maxdepth 1`, two-grammar `-name` pair) and at `emit_session_receipt` (same `PLANS_DIR` default). | Conductor: approve widening G2 (and `emit_session_receipt`) to a multi-root or index-driven closeout search; decide whether the unified plan index is the canonical resolver. |
